Germany Rebuilds its Armed Forces

Krupp Resigns from Industrial Guidance

To Devote Himself to his Duties

(Berlin) Mr. Krupp has recently been very busy with the task of re-arming Germany, so today he has resigned from his position as German industrial guide to devote himself to the task of re-arming Germany. Dr. Schacht, the president of the Deutsche Bank, has asked Mr. Hector of the Economic Association to serve as the German industrial guide. (17th Reuters Telegram)

German Minister to Austria, Papen, to be Dismissed

Returns to Serve as Special Commissioner for the Saar Region

(London) According to the "Daily Mail" reporter, the former Deputy Prime Minister Papen, the German Minister to Austria, will be removed from his post as Minister to Austria and return to serve as the Special Commissioner for the Saar region. (17th Havas Telegram)

British Cabinet Reported to be Reorganized

(London) According to the News Chronicle, the MacDonald Cabinet will be reorganized in early January next year. (17th Havas)

United States Considers Abandoning Freedom of the Seas Policy

President Plans to Request Authorization from Congress

To Decide on the Course to Take in Wartime

Anglo-American Cooperation Eliminates a Major Obstacle

(Washington) The United States' policy on freedom of the seas may soon change. Reuters learned today that the State Department will submit a carefully considered plan to President Roosevelt, advocating a modification of the inherent policy. This is related to the United States' right to maintain freedom of the seas as a neutral country in wartime. It is expected that the government will ask Congress to grant the President the power to act expediently in order to decide the course the United States should take in the event of war in other countries. It is heard that some parties agree that the United States will not protect any American ships that dare to enter the war zone during wartime. The purpose of this proposition is to avoid conflict. What the State Department is currently considering will of course receive President Roosevelt's approval. It is heard that this matter has nothing to do with the London naval talks. (16th Reuters Telegram)

(London) The British press is extremely interested in the possibility that the United States may abandon the principle of freedom of the seas, which it has always insisted on. The Daily Telegraph reported that "Freedom of the seas is a principle that the United States has always advocated, and the Allied navies often found it difficult to operate during the European War because this principle was an obstacle. Now that the United States has abandoned it, it is implementing a policy that aims to reduce excessive profits for merchants in wartime and to prevent war. Although it is not known whether the prevention of war will succeed, there is a benefit to abolishing the right of passage enjoyed by neutral countries in war zones, that is, if a war occurs, its duration can be shortened because the enemy country can strictly blockade it." The New Chronicle said, "President Roosevelt's decision is very important. This is tantamount to officially recognizing that there is no other way to guarantee world peace except for the collective security system. We can regard this as a movement for the United States to approach the League of Nations. What is even more important is that the principle of freedom of the seas has been the biggest obstacle to cooperation between Britain and the United States in the past. Now that the United States has abandoned this principle, it will not be difficult for Britain and the United States to cooperate closely, and Tokyo will inevitably pay attention to this." (17th Havas Telegram)

Hearst Newspapers Comment on the Status of the Philippines

Recognizes that Japan Will Ultimately Be a Hidden Danger to the United States

Granting Independence to the Philippines is Tantamount to Voluntarily Abandoning It

Strongly Criticizes the Short-Sightedness of Congressmen

(New York) The Hearst newspapers uniformly published a commentary signed by Hearst on the front page this morning, strongly criticizing Congress for passing the Philippine Independence Act. Hearst believes that the case is tantamount to abandoning the Philippine Islands to Japan. The article states that Japan's threat to the United States is undeniable. It is easy for Japan to occupy and manage the Philippine Islands. Once the time is right, it will annex the Philippine Islands and make them a part of the Japanese Empire. At this time, Japan's manpower and naval power will inevitably increase greatly. At this time, the Japanese can do whatever they want. Can Congress turn a blind eye to Japan's conspiracy to occupy the Philippine Islands, Guam, and trust territories and develop towards California? Japan is sure that Britain will do nothing but make empty protests. The article rebukes the cowardly congressmen, saying that they only know how to seek benefits for their constituencies. In their eyes, the few acres of farmland owned by one person in their constituency are more important than all the resources, commerce, and military value of the Philippine Islands. Hearst further stated that in 1935, whether traveling by American plane or Japanese plane from the Philippine Islands to California, it only takes twenty-four hours. And the day of abandoning the Philippine Islands is the day of the decline of the United States. Only corrupt countries shrink back, and only hardworking countries expand. Japan is now expanding, and thinking of this, I feel cold. (16th National Telegram)

US Army Chief's Annual Report Advocates Expanding the Air Force

Add 600 New Aircraft Within Three Years

Regular Armed Forces Currently Have 117,000

(New York) US Army Chief Bien today released his annual report, advocating that the United States should build more than 600 new aircraft in the next three years, and supporting the proposal that the US Air Force should have at least 2,320 new and suitable aircraft. The annual report also stated that as of the end of June, the United States' regular armed forces, excluding reserves, consisted of 12,212 officers and 117,000 soldiers. (16th Reuters Telegram)

Naval Talks Decide to Postpone Meeting on the Eve of Japan's Declaration of Treaty Abolition

The Three Countries Will Hold One Last Meeting

Whether to Continue or Not Depends on Japan's Attitude

US Representatives Prepare to Return Home at the End of the Month

(London) The naval talks between Britain, the United States, and Japan will probably be postponed until Thursday. It is expected that Japan will announce the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty on Friday or Saturday. The US representatives have scheduled to depart for home on the 29th of this month. The date for the continuation of the discussion has not been mentioned yet. This will depend on the outcome of the British and Japanese representatives' negotiations on the British proposal. The main point of the British plan is that all three parties announce their shipbuilding programs. If the negotiations between the British and Japanese representatives are expected to succeed, then they may continue to discuss with the US representatives. (17th Reuters Telegram)

(London) As far as the impressions gained by Davis, the chief representative of the United States in the naval talks, are concerned, the US delegation is unwilling to offer any promises or accept any restrictions if the naval talks are held again under the current circumstances. As for the mutual notification of naval shipbuilding programs by all countries, the US delegation admits that it is not qualified to discuss it and that it should be considered through diplomatic channels. The US delegation has now prepared everything so that it can depart from Southampton on the 29th of December and return home on the George Washington. Before the departure of the US delegation, the representatives of Britain, the United States, and Japan will hold a plenary meeting once. The meeting time should be before Japan announces the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty, probably on the 20th of this month. On that day, it will be officially announced that the naval talks will be postponed and a communique will be issued. (17th Havas Telegram)

Japan Sends Sato to Britain

To Strengthen the Lineup of the Delegation

Contents of the Anglo-Japanese Compromise Proposal

(London) Foreign Minister Hirota decided to send Sato Naotake, the ambassador to France, to London in the middle of this week to assist Ambassador Matsudaira, who also serves as the plenipotentiary for disarmament, because he is too busy day and night. He will continue to stay in London after the resumption of the talks to assist Matsudaira and Yamamoto, the two plenipotentiaries, to strengthen the lineup of the delegation and strive for the thorough implementation of Japan's new disarmament policy. When the formal meeting is held, he will of course attend as the plenipotentiary for foreign affairs. (17th Dentsu Telegram)

(London) Regarding the situation of the Anglo-Japanese compromise trial proposal, according to information from various sources, the general content is as follows:

(1) Each government must gradually reduce its shipbuilding plan over a period of five years. The content of the declaration is to clarify the details of the shipbuilding plan for each type of ship in terms of both quality and quantity, as well as the construction of replacement ships and the delay of replacement ships, etc., but it is completely autonomous and does not add any international constraints, and no trace of the ratio system may be left. (2) Based on the distinction between offensive force and defensive weapons, it is believed that the former has equality in the classification of ships, while the latter is based on the principle of total tonnage and considers the special circumstances of each country's defense. (A) Regarding battleships, aircraft carriers, and Class A cruisers, although the equality of the classification of ships can be confirmed, the naval power of Britain and Japan differs in reality, and it is necessary to wait for them to reach equilibrium. In fact, it takes a considerable number of years. Therefore, considering the above facts, the Japanese government should independently announce the shipbuilding stage in the next few years, such as five or ten years. (B) For defensive weapons below Class B cruisers, it is possible to recognize the necessary force based on the principle of total tonnage and according to the special characteristics of national defense. For example, the British government has a total of seventy Class A and Class B cruisers, including fifteen existing Class A cruisers and ten Class B large cruisers. It is necessary to maintain and recognize its forty-five ships below 7,000 tons. It is also necessary to recognize Japan's maintenance of its existing submarine force of 78,000 tons. Therefore, according to the London Treaty, the Japanese government has an obligation to reduce submarines to 53,700 tons by the end of 1936, while the compromise trial proposal recognizes the maintenance of the above tonnage and its replacement ships. (3) Regarding the proposal to set a maximum limit for the shipbuilding plan, the British government does not want to oppose it deliberately. Generally, it reduces the quality of offensive weapons by 30%, battleships to 25,000 tons, aircraft carriers to 20,000 tons, and cruisers to 7,000 tons. The tonnage obtained from the reduction in quality can be used for cruisers. Furthermore, the number of digits to reduce the existing force by a few points is determined by the maximum limit. The establishment of a common maximum limit means that France and Italy must also recognize their equality. Therefore, the British government intends to try to change the concept of a common maximum limit, and its declaration is completely free from the shackles of the ratio system. This is the latent hard work in the compromise trial proposal. Although the US representative has not yet expressed approval of the above compromise trial proposal, if the British and Japanese representatives formulate a concrete plan, then the US delegation will not be able to isolate itself from the outside world. Therefore, the British government authorities are still expecting that the US delegation will definitely participate in the compromise trial proposal. Thus, this compromise trial proposal has become the one that dominates the future trend of preparatory consultations. (17th Japan United Press Telegram)

Tokyo's Attitude is Cautious

Instructions to be Sent Out Today

Intention to Abolish the Naval Treaty is Determined

(Nanjing) At 3 p.m. today, Foreign Minister Hirota and Admiral Osumi

Page 7

visited Prime Minister Okada at his official residence to report on the situation of the London talks. Afterwards, the following plan was decided as a reply to the request for instructions from the two representatives Matsudaira and Yamamoto on the 13th, which will be sent out on the morning of the 18th. The content of the reply is as follows: (1) The Imperial Government has already put forward a new disarmament proposal and is working hard to conclude a new agreement, so it requests to continue the talks. (2) There is no objection to suspending the talks during Christmas, the end of the year, and the New Year, but it agrees to adjourn the meeting on the condition that the talks continue at an appropriate time next year. (3) During the adjournment, the British and American countries are requested to fully study and accept the Japanese proposal. (4) If the basic principles are recognized, it is prepared to submit specific figures. (17th Dentsu Telegram)

(Tokyo) After meeting with Prime Minister Okada, Admiral Osumi said that the talks with the Prime Minister did not involve the issue of abolishing the Washington Treaty. Japan's policy has not changed in any way with regard to the established policy. If it is passed at the Privy Council plenary meeting on the 19th, it will proceed accordingly, and there is no obstacle to this. (17th Dentsu Telegram)

(Tokyo) The Japanese government has roughly decided to announce the abolition of the treaty on the 22nd. At the same time, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs decided to issue a statement, the content of which is roughly as follows: (1) The abolition of the treaty is Japan's right, and because it is not suitable for the current situation, the abolition of the treaty is beyond doubt. (2) Japan hopes to conclude a new agreement again, so the abolition of the treaty does not violate the spirit of disarmament. (3) Announcing the abolition of the treaty will not hinder the initial London talks. (17th China United Press Telegram)

Naval Preliminary Negotiations Show Discord Among Three Nations

(Tokyo) The outcome of the London Naval Conference negotiations is truly worth contemplating. It is said that the British side, before the Washington Treaty's abrogation notice, wants to take advantage of the Christmas holiday to conclude the meeting satisfactorily. The American side wants Japan to bear the responsibility for the breakdown of the talks when Japan gives notice of the treaty's abrogation. The current position of the Japanese side is to drop the "abrogation notice" bomb. Therefore, the differing positions of the United Kingdom, the United States and Japan are as follows:

(1) On the Washington Treaty issue, Japan advocates abrogation, while the United Kingdom and the United States advocate preservation. (1) On the issue of equal rights, Japan advocates autonomous armament equal rights and equality of national defense security. The United Kingdom and the United States believe that this would undermine equality of national defense security and advocate proportionalism. (1) On the issue of restrictions on armaments methods and holdings, Japan advocates abolishing the differential ratios by warship type, setting a common maximum holding quantity, major reductions in offensive forces, and reductions in total holdings. The United States advocates preserving the existing treaty and reducing holdings by 20% based on differential proportionalism. The United Kingdom hopes to preserve the existing treaty, requiring the holding of seventy lower-tier cruisers and advocating considerable reductions based on qualitative restrictions. (1) On the issue of warship type restrictions, Japan divides between offensive and defensive types. The United States advocates the warship types of the current treaty. Although the United Kingdom recognizes increasing the interchangeability between warship types, it maintains the existing warship types. (1) On the issue of qualitative restrictions, Japan, with substantive equality as a condition, advocates reducing warship tonnage and armament caliber. The United States firmly advocates restricting laws based on the existing system of battleship and big gun doctrine. The United Kingdom advocates reducing the single-ship tonnage of each warship type by 30% and reducing armament caliber. (Seventeenth Day Electric News)

Turkey and Greece Hold Talks

Not Limited to Geneva Work

Also Covers Minority Issues

Athens Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü Aras returned from Geneva and came here to meet with Greek Prime Minister Tsaldaris and Foreign Minister Maximos. It is reported that the talks between the two countries will not be limited to the work in Geneva and the clothing issue of Turkish religious clerics. The Greek side also seeks to take the opportunity to resolve various issues related to the Greek minority within Turkey in order to eliminate the causes of disputes between the two countries and enhance amity. (Sixteenth Day Havas Dispatch)

Saar Unfortunate Incident: British Officer Suspended Pending Investigation

Public Anger Difficult to Defy, Suffered Severe Beating

Advance Party of British Police Heads to Saar

Saarbrücken Since the arrival of the international police force here, the first case occurred this evening. A British officer has been suspended pending investigation as a result. According to the announcement, a British officer, Jestyce, while turning his car on the road, hit a pedestrian on the sidewalk. A crowd gathered and took a hostile attitude toward the three people in the car, especially Jestyce, for reasons unknown. A conflict then arose, with several shots fired. One person was shot in the abdomen. Jestyce was beaten and is currently being treated in the hospital. An investigation is underway, and after the results are available, a report will be submitted to the police tribunal ordered to handle this case to punish all persons involved according to law, regardless of their position. At the same time, according to a Berlin Reuters correspondent, the deputy leader of the German Frontline, Nittmann, is said to have filed a protest with the plebiscite committee regarding this case, demanding the punishment of the police officers involved. According to unofficial sources, Jestyce and two friends were driving in a car. During a U-turn, they drove too far and injured the foot of a woman. Onlookers gathered quickly, their demeanor fierce. Jestyce then took out his credentials, claiming to be an officer of the international police force, and asked the crowd to disperse. This further angered the crowd. Jestyce then brandished his pistol at the crowd. Several people snatched his weapon. During the struggle, two bullets flew out, hitting one person in the abdomen, but the injury was not serious. Police rushed to the scene and worked hard to restore order, rescuing Jestyce and his two friends. The three suffered multiple abrasions on their hands and faces, but none were serious. Jestyce later told a Reuters reporter that he had fired a shot into the ground before the crowd snatched his gun, and that the bullets flying out was accidental. He and his friends were all in plain clothes at the time. (Sixteenth Day Reuters Dispatch)

Course of Events

Saarbrücken Details have emerged regarding the unfortunate incident that occurred here at 3 AM this morning. A car carrying three people was driving very fast and crashed into a crowd of pedestrians. The driver was a British police officer, who had been deployed to the Saar region as a special officer several weeks ago. It is said that the incident was caused by the driver being intoxicated and losing control. Four people were knocked down and severely injured. According to eyewitnesses, onlookers immediately called the police and blocked the car from moving forward, saying that it should not be released until the police had investigated. The police officer intended to drive away, and when onlookers stepped forward to stop him, the police officer fired two shots at the crowd, injuring one person. When he tried to fire a third shot, the gun was knocked out of his hand. He continued to rant and rave until he was subdued by the crowd. After the incident, the local people protested loudly, demanding that the authorities punish the police officer.

Proclamation to the People

Saar Governing Commission

The following proclamation was then issued: "On the night of December 16, a police officer attempted to turn his car on Goebbels Street and inadvertently crashed into a sidewalk, injuring pedestrians. A crowd gathered and, without knowing the circumstances, protested against the people in the car, especially the police officer. A conflict then arose, resulting in shots being fired and one person being injured in the abdomen. The police officer was also beaten by the crowd and sent to the hospital for treatment. After the police authorities have investigated the matter in detail, a report will be submitted to the court for handling. The police authorities will not show any favoritism. Pending a thorough investigation of the case, the British police officer has been temporarily suspended from duty.

German Indignation

The Deputy Director of the German Avant-Garde Corps, Mr. Nittmann, visited the Dutch member of the Saar Plebiscite Commission to protest the illegal actions of the British police officer and solemnly declared that the police officer was not affiliated with the international police force, demanding that the police officer be severely punished to prevent similar incidents from occurring again.

Urging Calm

Nittmann also gave a speech during the day to 50,000 Germans in the Saar region, repeatedly urging them to remain calm and saying that we should not regard the police officer's individual actions as the norm in his country. We should know that the United Kingdom may not approve of this action either. However, after this incident, our position should become clearer, and we should pay special attention to selecting qualified personnel in the future to avoid the recurrence of similar unfortunate events. We should adapt to circumstances and fight to the end without fear of hardship. Even if axes and saws are in front of us, we will not care because soon we will be able to return to our motherland. (Seventeenth Day National Telegram)

Another Dispute

Saarbrücken Saar is now in a tense situation due to two disputes. British police officer Jestyce had his head smashed by a German crowd and is in critical condition. He is currently being treated in the hospital. At the same time, there was also a disturbance in a cafe, stemming from a conflict between the head of the British police contingent in the Saar region, Hessler, and Prince Löwenstein. The authorities are unwilling to announce the details, but it is said that Prince Löwenstein has already requested the chairman of the League of Nations Saar Governing Commission, Knox, to remove Hessler from his position. (Sixteenth Day National Telegram)

British Troops Deploy

(London) The advance party of British soldiers participating in the Saar international police force boarded a ship in Dover today to go to Calais on their way to the Saar. Crowds lined the pier to see them off. The soldiers cheered in response. The commander of the international police force, British Major General Brindell, and the commanders of the Swedish contingent, General Hoist, and the Dutch contingent, General Løwegiessen, have all arrived in Saarbrücken. Only the commander of the Italian contingent, Viscount Plascag, has not yet arrived. All of the police force is expected to arrive in Saarbrücken before Christmas. Local shops and entertainment venues are happy at the prospect of increased business. The German commander Brindell is currently consulting with the chairman of the Saar Administrative Commission, Knox, on how to allocate the troops throughout the region. (Sixteenth Day Reuters Dispatch)

Italian Government Sends Note to League of Nations Refuting Abyssinian Protest

Proves That Abyssinian Troops Actually Initiated Hostilities

Opposes Arbitration, Demands Compensation and Apology

Italian Minister to Abyssinia Returns Home

Rome The Italian government has sent a notification to the League of Nations regarding the dispute between Italy and Abyssinia in order to prove that the aggression on December 5 was committed by Abyssinia. It states that Walwal has always been within the territory of Italian Somaliland and that Italian troops have occupied the area for many years. Recently, an Abyssinian police officer led a guard of more than 1,000 people protecting the Anglo-Abyssinian Boundary Commission and attempted to enter the area, claiming to the garrison commander that the residents of the area were Abyssinian citizens. The Italian garrison commander refused, and the members of the Boundary Commission withdrew, but the guard remained stationed in front of Walwal, plotting to incite the indigenous troops in the area to desert. On December 5, the Abyssinian troops attacked the Italian garrison without provocation, causing heavy losses. The Italian garrison resisted on the spot and mobilized reinforcements. When the reinforcements arrived, they launched a counterattack in cooperation with airplanes and tanks. The Abyssinian troops then began to flee. After the incident, the Italian government protested to the Abyssinian government and reserved the right to demand an apology and compensation. The Abyssinian government requested that the case be submitted to an arbitration court in accordance with the 1928 Italo-Abyssinian treaty. The Italian government replied that the incident occurred within Italian territory, and the situation was clear. There was no doubt that the matter should be submitted to arbitration. Therefore, the Italian government still maintains that Abyssinia should quickly fulfill the apology and compensation measures. (Sixteenth Day Havas Dispatch)

Naples, Italy The Italian Minister to Abyssinia, Vinci, returned from the capital of Abyssinia. After landing here, he took a car to Rome. Although the Italian Minister did not make any statement, his return home is clearly related to the conflict between Italy and Abyssinia in the Walwal area. (Sixteenth Day Havas Dispatch)

Bulgarian Communists Plot Revolution

Plot Exposed, 500 Arrested

Sofia About 500 Communists have been arrested in the Zeskoff area of Bulgaria, a tobacco-producing region. 175 of them are local militiamen who conspired with the Communists to cause unrest. Detailed revolutionary plans were found at the headquarters of the rebels. According to the plan, the rebels planned to seize the weapons of the army and kill the officers when they rose up. Documents and pamphlets inciting the rebellion were also found in the arsenal. It is said that the leader is the well-known Communist Stov, who a few weeks ago looted the local treasury and wealthy families in the village of Austerlitz with his accomplices. The criminals were captured a few days later in their deep mountain bandit lair, and their conspiracy plan was exposed as a result. (Seventeenth Day National Telegram)

Bolivian Troops Fully Mobilize, a Last Stand

Buenos Aires, Argentina Official news here today says that Paraguayan troops have occupied the Fort Alcotendanal and will soon be completely victorious. At the same time, Bolivia has ordered the full mobilization of its reserve forces, preparing to make a last stand against the enemy. Russia Executes Two More People

(Moscow) Russia has executed many people since discovering the so-called terrorist acts against Soviet officials, and it has not yet ended. Today, four more people were sentenced to death, including two people, one named Ushakov, the son of a clergyman, and the other named Sanin, said to be a bandit. They were charged with murdering two 15-year-old girls and robbing a collective farm. The other two were accomplices. (Sixteenth Day Reuters Dispatch)

Asia Minor Earthquake

Istanbul Anatolia, also known as Asia Minor, was hit by several earthquakes last night, causing significant loss of life and property. The tremors continued until midnight. During the first tremor, residents rushed into the streets and other places in fear to avoid being crushed to death by collapsing houses, but many people were unable to escape and were crushed by collapsing walls. It is estimated that about 20 men and women died. In addition, more than 100 people were injured, some of whom were seriously injured and may not survive. It is now estimated that at least 25 villages and towns have been destroyed, leaving tens of thousands of people homeless. After receiving reports of the disaster, the government immediately began organizing disaster relief efforts and transported cotton, food, medicine, and other supplies to the disaster area for distribution. It is reported that several areas in the disaster area are in urgent need of assistance because all of their food supplies have been lost in the earthquake. (Seventeenth Day Reuters Dispatch)

Roosevelt Becomes More Right-Wing

New York Wall Street today gradually believes that President Roosevelt and his New Deal will become more right-wing in the next few days than before. This right-wing shift has begun, but it has not yet reached its peak. It is said that in order to save face, this change will be accomplished with extreme caution. It is claimed that huge public debts are a major problem for the government. The chairman of Chase Bank, Atley, advocates direct relief and that states and society share part of the funding. Atley opposes work relief because it is uneconomical. Many states have stopped local relief efforts, and all expenses are now borne by the central county government. Experts here declare that saving waste and balancing the budget will automatically stabilize the dollar, while huge public works expenditures and other government measures are considered wasteful. The purpose of public works is work relief. Wall Street merchants now believe that private commerce has catered to President Roosevelt's policies and that the government and big business are cooperating. It is stated here that since the giants of industry and commerce have joined hands with Roosevelt, the concept of industry and commerce has changed. This trend can be seen in the recovery of commerce. (Sixteenth Day National Telegram)

(Washington) Senator Costigan said today that improving the government's silver purchase law and expanding the effect of gold and silver to increase the value of gold and silver will be the main points of the proposals of liberals in the next Congress. Liberal members will also devote themselves to construction work, increasing the government's power to control funds and currency. Other points in the proposal are as follows: (1) Expand public works projects, use work relief methods to provide unemployed workers with a guarantee of life. (2) Pass social security legislation. (3) Pass bills to prevent patents and weaken the activities of some current patents. (4) Pass bills to protect the right of workers to negotiate in groups, and to have workers elect representatives, denying company unions. (5) Continue to consider veterans' benefits, but did not mention immediately paying veterans' allowances. (6) Recommend to the government to amend the constitution to ban tax-exempt securities. (7) Pass a bill to reduce electricity bills and expand federal and local government electricity plans. (Sixteenth Day National Telegram)

Clara Bow Gives Birth

Santa Monica, USA Silver screen star Clara Bow gave birth to a child weighing eight pounds in a hospital here today. Her husband, Rex Bell, is also a silver screen star. (Sixteenth Day National Telegram)

Nanking Municipal Government Memorial Week: Shi Ying Reports on the Meaning of Equal Rights

(Nanking) Shi Ying reported on the most important proposal of the Fifth Plenary Session at the Municipal Government Memorial Week this morning, that is, the telegram from Wang and Chiang, which has been passed by the meeting. Its content is to separate the powers and responsibilities of the central and local governments in detail. Internal disputes will absolutely not use force in the future, but use political methods to seek solutions. Since the 17th year, foreign troubles have deepened and the Red disaster has become more urgent. Although the communist bandits in Jiangxi have been wiped out, the bandit troubles in Sichuan and other places are still fierce. The root of the trouble is still that internal affairs are not perfect. Now the government authorities feel that the powers and responsibilities of the central and local governments should be separated in detail in order to increase political efficiency, and the reform of domestic politics, it is not too late to make amends. (Seventeenth Day Special Dispatch)

Many Nanking Stores Also Sell Lottery Tickets

(Nanking) The commercial situation in Nanking is extremely sluggish. Many stores are using speculative business to make up for operating losses. Recently, money, rice, cigarette stores, banks and bookstores have also been selling lottery tickets. Because they can enjoy a 95% discount on pure profits as agents, the [Yellow Disaster] [Aviation] and other lottery tickets are filling the market. There are more than 3,000 large and small agencies throughout the city. The end of the year is approaching, and there are many buyers, so the income from this side business is almost more profitable than the main business. (Seventeenth Day Special Dispatch)

Former Ministry of Communications Site to Be Used by Ordnance Department

Statistics on Drought Losses in Zhejiang Province

(Hangzhou) This year's drought in Zhejiang Province, excluding Leqing, Pingyang, Ruian, and Yuehuan counties, affected 71 counties. The average harvest was 50%. It is estimated that the total area of affected farmland was 17,938,114 mu. The drought reduced the grain harvest by 34,628,812 dan, resulting in a loss of 138,515,280 yuan. The yield of miscellaneous grains was reduced by 5,329,451 dan, resulting in a loss of 10,658,902 yuan. The total loss is estimated at 149,741,182 yuan, affecting 18,314,217 people. (Special Dispatch, 17th)

Legislative Yuan Passes County Autonomy Law

The Legislative Yuan held its 85th regular meeting on the afternoon of the 17th and passed the County Autonomy Law. The full text is as follows:

Chapter 1: Autonomous Regions

Article 1: The county is an autonomous unit, and its territory shall be based on its existing territory.

Article 2: The establishment of a county and changes to its territory shall be subject to the approval of the National Government.

Article 3: Below the county are townships. The organization within townships and towns, neighboring areas, local natural conditions, or customs, and the division and organization of townships and towns may be appropriately changed.

Where the county government is located, it may be divided into several districts. Districts are at the same level as townships and towns, and their organization is the same.

Article 4: The demarcation or change of the areas in the preceding article shall be subject to the approval of the provincial government and reported to the Ministry of the Interior for record.

Chapter 2: County Autonomy Matters

Article 5: County autonomy matters are as follows: (1) County household registration investigation and registration matters; (2) County land administration matters; (3) County financial matters; (4) County transportation, water conservancy, and other engineering construction matters; (5) County public and cooperative matters; (6) County police and security matters; (7) County education and culture matters; (8) County health matters; (9) County conservation and relief matters; (10) County public property management and organization matters; (11) County historical sites preservation matters; (12) Other matters belonging to county autonomy.

Chapter 3: County Citizens

Article 6: Citizens of the Republic of China, regardless of gender, who have resided continuously within the county for more than one year, or who have resided for more than two years, and who are over the age of twenty, and who have registered after taking an oath, are county citizens and have the right to attend the county citizen's congress, the township citizen's congress, the town citizen's congress, and the district citizen's congress, and to exercise the rights of election, recall, initiative, and referendum.

Article 7: The oath and registration in the preceding article shall be held at the township office, town office, or district office. The measures shall be determined by the Ministry of the Interior.

Article 8: The procedures for county citizens to exercise the four powers of election, recall, initiative, and referendum shall be determined separately.

Chapter 4: County Citizens' Congress

Article 9: The County Citizens' Congress is organized by county citizens and exercises the rights of election, recall, initiative, and referendum.

Article 10: The County Citizens' Congress shall be held once every three years. Temporary county citizens' congresses may be held when necessary. The County Citizens' Congress shall be held on the same day in separate venues in each township, town, and district.

Article 11: The County Citizens' Congress or temporary County Citizens' Congress shall be convened by the county magistrate. However, when it is held for the election or recall of the county magistrate, or for other matters in which the county magistrate should recuse himself, it shall be convened by the speaker of the county council.

When one-third or more of the townships, towns, and districts in the county jointly propose to the county magistrate or the speaker of the county council to convene a temporary county citizen's congress, each having at least one-twentieth of the total number of citizens, the county magistrate or speaker shall convene it immediately. Article 12: The County Citizens' Congress or temporary County Citizens' Congress shall only become effective when one-half or more of the townships, towns, and districts in the county are present, each having at least one-tenth of the total number of citizens, and with the consent of more than half of the citizens present.

The resolution in the preceding paragraph shall be announced by the convener.

Chapter 5: County Council

Article 13: A county council shall be established in the county, which shall be organized by county councilors elected by the county citizens' congress.

Article 14: The number of county councilors shall be seven in counties with a population of less than 50,000, nine in counties with a population of 50,000 or more but less than 100,000, eleven in counties with a population of 100,000 or more but less than 150,000, thirteen in counties with a population of 150,000 or more but less than 200,000, and one additional county councilor shall be elected for every 30,000 people in counties with a population of 200,000 or more, but the maximum shall not exceed 30.

Article 15: The term of office of county councilors is three years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 16: The powers of the county council are as follows: (1) To discuss and decide on the county budget and review the county final accounts; (2) To discuss and decide on county taxes and contracts that increase the county treasury's burden; (3) To discuss and decide on the management and disposal of county-owned property; (4) To audit county finances; (5) To discuss and decide on county single regulations; (6) To make suggestions to the county government on the county's political development matters; (7) To discuss and decide on matters submitted by the county magistrate; (8) To question the county magistrate; (9) To accept petitions from county citizens; (10) Other powers conferred by law.

Article 17: County councilors may not concurrently serve as officials of the county government or its subordinate agencies.

Article 18: County councilors are unpaid, but during the meeting period, travel expenses may be given according to local circumstances.

Article 19: The county council shall have one speaker and one deputy speaker, who shall be elected by the county councilors by secret ballot.

When the speaker or deputy speaker is vacant due to an accident, a by-election shall be held immediately.

Article 20: When the county council is in session, the speaker shall preside. If the speaker is unable to preside, the deputy speaker shall preside. If both the speaker and deputy speaker are unable to preside, the councilors shall elect one of themselves as the temporary chairman.

Article 21: The county council shall hold a regular meeting once every six months, but a temporary meeting shall be convened immediately at the request of the county magistrate or one-third or more of the county councilors.

The duration of regular and temporary meetings shall not exceed one month.

Article 22: The county council shall not be able to hold a meeting without the attendance of more than half of the councilors. The voting on proposals shall be carried out with the consent of more than half of the councilors present. In the event of a tie, the chairman shall decide.

Article 23: When the county council is in session, the county magistrate may be invited to attend and report or explain.

Article 24: The county magistrate shall execute the resolutions of the county council. If the county magistrate believes that the resolution is inappropriate, he may submit it for reconsideration with detailed reasons. If two-thirds or more of the councilors present still insist on the original resolution, the county magistrate shall execute it immediately. If the execution is delayed, the county council may convene a county citizen's congress to decide whether or not to recall the county magistrate.

If the recall in the preceding paragraph is rejected by the county citizens' congress, the county council shall immediately hold a new election.

Article 25: County councilors shall not be held responsible to the outside world for speeches and votes made during meetings.

Article 26: County councilors shall not be arrested or detained during the session, except in cases of flagrant offense, without the permission of the county council.

Article 27: County councilors who violate the law or neglect their duties shall be recalled by the county citizens' congress.

Article 28: The county council shall have one secretary-general and two to four secretaries, who shall, under the command of the speaker, handle records, documents, accounting, and general affairs. During the meeting period, the county council may employ employees as appropriate.

Article 29: The rules of procedure for the county council shall be determined by the county council. (End of text)

Stagnant Production and Sales of Tung Oil in Zhejiang Province

Affected by Stagnation of Foreign Firms in Hankou

Quzhou Correspondence: Silk, tea, and tung oil have always been the main export products of Zhejiang Province. In recent years, silk and tea have been far behind Japan and India/Ceylon, respectively, and have been subject to the low-price dumping of their products, causing business to plummet. However, tung oil has been able to maintain its inherent sales channels due to demand from Europe and the United States. Among the tung oil-producing areas in China, Zhejiang is second only to Sichuan and Hunan. The producing areas are distributed in Chun'an, Sui'an, Yuqian, Changhua, Shouchang, Changshan, Jiangshan, Dongyang, Yiwu, Jinhua, Lanxi, Yongkang, Zhuji, Wuyi, Fenshui, Qu County, Longquan, Songyang, Pingyang, and other counties in eastern and western Zhejiang. The areas are characterized by poor land and impoverished people, and planting tung trees is regarded as the only sideline. Oil pressing operations have flourished in response to demand from all sides. In the past decade, Zhejiang tung oil has formed a three-legged stand with Sichuan and Hunan in domestic and foreign markets, and has gradually become one of Zhejiang's emerging industries, surpassing silk and tea trade. However, future concerns lie in the poor quality of tung seed pressing and the impurity of the oil, which may lead to the elimination of European and American sales. This year, the tung seeds in the producing areas of Chun'an, Changhua, and Yuqian in western Zhejiang, and Lanxi, Yongkang, Jiangshan, and Changshan in eastern Zhejiang, were affected by the severe drought in the summer and autumn, resulting in less fruit and lower oil content. According to estimates by tung planting farmers in the producing areas, the total output of tung seeds in the province this year is about 100,000 dan less than last year, resulting in a significant loss in rural income. Currently, farmers in Lanxi, Jiangshan, and other places have successively organized production cooperatives in order to improve tung oil production and promote European and American markets, jointly seeking development. As for the current sales situation, due to the stagnation of foreign firms in Hankou, the Hangzhou market has followed suit, and only sporadic transactions are taking place in Shanghai, with no large-scale shipments for export. All kinds of goods have arrived at the docks and are languishing in warehouses, with few inquiries. Although US sales have recently increased, pushing up prices in Hankou, domestic sales in the province have fallen, and market prices are only around 26.4 yuan, remaining stagnant. Both production and sales are trending towards a downturn. (12th)

Songjiang: The Educational Community Upholds Justice in the Fenglong Temple Case

Songjiang County Bailongtan Elementary School has been repeatedly disturbed by monks from the Xichan Temple over the Fenglong Temple issue, and the principal has been falsely accused. Details have been recorded in previous reports. It is now known that the educational community in the county, including the County High School, County Teachers' School, Seventh Women's Teachers' School, Provincial Songjiang Elementary School, and Guanyinqiao, Yangjiaqiao, Xidu, Huayang, Mojialong, and other elementary schools, unanimously uphold justice, and jointly sent a telegram to County Governor Jin, requesting the punishment of the monks as a warning against future offenses and to maintain education.

Kunshan: Murder Case Occurs in Zhendong Village

Dozens of households of Guangdong people live in Zhendong Village outside the East Gate. They also formed a Zhendong Company. Kuang, the stepmother of Ma Zuojun, a shareholder of the company, is 35 years old and has lived there with DeMin, the son of the former wife, for a long time. However, the mother and son had different opinions and often quarreled. The other night, Kuang was suddenly shot to death with a hunting gun in the middle of the night, and DeMin's whereabouts are unknown. Neighbors noticed and reported to Ma Ming, the representative of the company, who reported to the county government. This morning at 9 o'clock, Judge Zhang led the inspectors to the village for inspection. It was found that Kuang had twelve gunshot wounds near her left hip, penetrating deep into the bones. There were nine gunshot wounds next to her birth canal, and eighteen bullet exit points on her right trousers, all with torn skin. It was determined that she had been shot and killed with a gun before her death. The coroner completed the report and returned to the county to issue an arrest warrant to investigate the murderer.

Police Officer Drowns While Arresting Gamblers

On the 27th of last month, the police from the Malu Public Security Substation were dispatched to arrest gamblers at the home of Lu Wenhuan in Chejiabang, but they were resisted, resulting in the drowning death of police officer Liu Tianwu. Afterwards, the county bureau detained more than ten people, including Zhou Wenyuan and Gu Shixian. After repeated interrogations by Director Wu, they were sent to the county for handling. Unexpectedly, Gu Shixian accused Director Wu of illegal torture to the county government and requested an injury examination. After the county examination, he published the process in the newspaper. Although someone has recently mediated, it has not been completely resolved. Unexpectedly, the other night, Wu Siqin in Mantoubang (8th District) held a wedding for his nephew-in-law, and relatives and friends gathered to gamble. The director of the sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau, Bao Renzhai, found out and immediately dispatched police to arrest them. It is not known how, but a dispute arose with the Wu family. Residents of the neighboring village mistakenly thought it was robbery and gathered the crowd, causing police officer Liu Jinshan to fall into the river and drown again. Afterwards, Director Bao found out and urgently reported to the county bureau, which reported to the county government. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang was commissioned to go to the village for inspection. The county bureau also sent people to investigate the beginning and end of the matter, and then conduct further investigation.

Jiading: Two Families Robbed in Yao Dun Bridge

Shen Guisheng, a resident of Yaodun Bridge in the North Guang Township of the First District, operates a military uniform factory in Shanghai and is quite prosperous. His brother was to be married on the 17th. On the evening of the 15th, he bought a large number of wedding supplies in Shanghai and brought them back to his hometown. At about 2 or 3 AM that night, fourteen bandits, each holding flashlights and pistols, broke into the door and forced Shen to hand over the hidden gold. He was robbed of more than 700 yuan in cash and clothing. Shen's brother's bride was Shen Ayun's daughter, who lived in the same house. The bandits then went to Ayun's house to search for clothing and other items. They left around 4 o'clock. The losses of the two families were more than 2,000 gold.

Wuxi: This Year's Silk Factory Survey

Among the machine industries in this county, the yarn industry was established the earliest, and the silk reeling industry has the most factories. The years of 1926 and 1927 were the most prosperous period, with a total of 54 factories in the county. Among them, three were never established, and one was established and reorganized into a cloth factory. There are currently 50 factories in existence. Only 12 factories operated throughout the year, 24 factories operated intermittently, and 14 factories never operated. There are a total of 14,114 silk reeling machines. When all factories are operating, 42,246 male and female workers are required, with female workers accounting for 90% of the total. Although 11,182 machines operated this year, the shortest operation lasted for less than a month. Except for 12 factories such as Huaxin, Yongchun, Jinji, Yongsheng, Longchang, and Minfeng, the rest only operated for two or three months. 13 factories, such as Yuchang, Yuankang, Jinfeng, Qianyuan, Yongyu, Jingcheng, Nanchang, Yongfu, Runxingsheng, Hengyi, Fucheng, Yunda, and Huiyuan, were unable to operate from beginning to end. Therefore, the number of male and female workers employed by these factories this year is less than two-thirds of the peak period. This is the reason for the sluggish market in Xiyi and the difficult life of the workers.

A Dramatic Fight Between Monks, Nuns, and a Band of Thieves at Fucheng Temple

In the vicinity of Datun Bridge near the Ninth Branch of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, there is a temple called Fucheng Temple. After the former abbot, Monk De'en, passed away due to illness, his disciple, Leng Qing, took over the management of the temple. Recently, Leng Qing specially invited Monk Changzhao from Kaiyuan Temple in Shaoxing to come to the temple to chant the Seven Buddhas Sutra. Unexpectedly, at about 10 p.m. the day before yesterday, seven or eight thugs suddenly broke in to rob the temple. At that time, Changzhao had not yet fallen asleep and, upon learning of the robbery, grabbed his Zen staff and fiercely fought the thieves. The nun Leng Qing, upon hearing the commotion, also rushed to help in the fight. However, due to being outnumbered, Changzhao suffered eight cuts to his head by the thieves, and Leng Qing was also cut three times. Afterwards, they reported the incident to the Ninth Branch for investigation, but no one was apprehended. Only a hat left behind by the bandits was recovered and reported to the General Bureau for verification. Yesterday, the two monks and nuns were admitted to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. Also, in Zhouxiang Village, Xintang Township, Second District, the home of farmer Zhou Yinrong was raided by eight local bandits who broke down the door and robbed over ten dan (a unit of dry weight) of japonica rice. Yinrong was also beaten and injured. The villagers then sounded the gong to surround and apprehend the bandits, who were eventually scared off. The government is handling the case.

Changzhou: Second Annual County-Wide Cross-Country Race

The second annual cross-country race in Wujin County, which had been in preparation for a long time, was held on the afternoon of the 16th. Ninety-three people registered to participate, but only fifty-four actually competed. The starting point of the race was the Rainbow Bridge inside Wenzai Gate, and the finish line was on the road outside Wenzai Gate, a total distance of eight kilometers. At about 2 p.m., the athletes gathered at the starting point. The chief referee and commander, Si Daoping, gave the order, and with a bang, the athletes sprinted forward. Zhang Xuecheng was the first to reach the finish line, with a time of thirty-two minutes and 4/5 of a second, winning the championship. Cao Yaobin was the runner-up, followed by Zhu Qingyun in third place, Leng Dune in fourth, Min Junxiang in fifth, Sha Zhengshang in sixth, Zhang Zhixian in seventh, Xu Jiacheng in eighth, Gu Jinwu in ninth, and Yuan Jinwen in tenth. After the race, an awards ceremony was held at the public sports field. County Magistrate Hou gave a speech before presenting the awards, and then photos were taken before the event concluded.

Jiaxing: Head of Second Branch Dismissed for Case

During the Qingming Festival this year in Jiaxing, at the dragon boat race held in Wangjiangjing Town under the jurisdiction of the county, the local police officers failed to maintain order and instead collected fees from the vendors, resulting in a tragic incident in which over twenty men and women were trampled to death on Changhong Bridge. Subsequently, someone reported the dereliction of duty of Chen Riyuan, the head of the Third Public Security Bureau, to the provincial authorities. He was then ordered to be transferred to the position of head of the Second Public Security Bureau of the county. It has now been learned that the Civil Affairs Department has confirmed the county's report that Chen Riyuan was indeed derelict in his duties and should be dismissed from his current position as head of the Second Public Security Bureau as punishment. Wang Shouhe has been appointed to fill the vacancy. After receiving the appointment, Wang arrived at the bureau yesterday to take over his duties.

Hangzhou: Forty Bandits Escorted to the Province

The attempted disturbance by the Red Bandits in Suian, Zhejiang, was crushed by the Security Corps, who captured forty suspects, including Red Bandit suspects and local ruffians like Zhou Wangfu, who took advantage of the situation to rob. Yesterday (the 17th), they were escorted to the province by the county's Security Corps. Among them, one named Jiang Dachang died in the car due to illness, and his body was left in front of the Provincial Security Office. In the afternoon, the Hangzhou District Court sent personnel to examine the body and provide a coffin. The remaining criminals were all escorted to the Army Prison for interrogation.

Xiaoshan: Account Boat Robbed in Xixiaojiang River

On the night of the 16th, an account boat travelling from Shaoxing to Linpu in Xiaoshan was robbed in the Xixiaojiang River. The boat carried two shop assistants from a rice store and over 250 yuan in cash. Unexpectedly, when passing the Luomenchen area, they were intercepted by two pirate boats. The pirates silenced the shop assistants and boarded the boat to loot. All the cash was taken, as well as the shop assistants’ silk gowns and scarves. One shop assistant, in an attempt to protect his cotton coat, was stabbed five times in the leg by a bandit with a sharp knife, causing profuse bleeding and causing him to fall unconscious. The victim has reported the incident to the police in Keqiao and Linpu, requesting their cooperation in the investigation.

Special Article

Reflections on Anti-Chinese Sentiments: Considering Their Friends and Foes

By Zhou Qigang

In recent times, the cries of anti-Chinese sentiment from various regions have reached our ears and manifested before our eyes. The noise seems to grow louder every day. In summary, the content boils down to two points: (1) The world's economic panic in recent years has become unbearable, leading to a symbolic perspective of forceful seizure, thus creating a localized misunderstanding of overseas Chinese. (2) Forgetting historical facts and neglecting the interdependent conditions of human existence, resulting in putting the cart before the horse and delusional incitement.

Regarding the former: The world's economic panic of recent years is indeed very different in nature from previous cyclical panics of capitalism. Whether in terms of degree, scope, or continuity, the foundation of the panic is built on general crises. From capitalist countries, it affects the agricultural economy of colonies, causing it to synchronize with the panic of capitalist countries and fall into a deep recession. In places shrouded in this atmosphere of economic panic, merchants go bankrupt, workers lose their jobs, and farmers teeter on the brink of starvation. They all suffer the pain of bankruptcy, unemployment, and hunger, but seeing the unique resilience and hard work of overseas Chinese, who can still struggle to survive in harsh environments, they often cannot overcome the base instinct of jealousy. They blindly transfer their resentment onto the overseas Chinese, believing that worldly possessions are acquired through seizure, not through the rewards of labor. Thus, the agricultural, industrial, and commercial activities of the overseas Chinese are resented by those who live without labor, leading to a sense of dissatisfaction with the overseas Chinese. This subconscious jealousy arises, causing great losses to everyone. Perhaps the losses are even greater in places where anti-Chinese sentiment is more severe.

Amidst this economic downturn, the losses suffered by the overseas Chinese are significant. According to statistics from last year, only 132,000 people emigrated from our country, while 278,000 overseas Chinese returned. This is a decrease of 146,000 people in one year. The amount of remittances sent back to China by overseas Chinese has also been greatly reduced. Last year, it decreased from about 200 million yuan to 80-90%. The significant losses suffered by the overseas Chinese and our national economy are undeniable, and the losses suffered by the various places of residence are also considerable, especially in places with anti-Chinese sentiment, where the economic situation is even more precarious. This putting the cart before the horse will only harm oneself and make things worse!

The sacrifices of the overseas Chinese are indeed their price, but according to our calculations, whether what the overseas Chinese gain is worth the price is questionable. Moreover, whether other nations can compare to the results of this price is another question. According to recent statistics, there are approximately 8 to 10 million overseas Chinese. Based on the number of years and deaths, assuming there are currently 10 million overseas Chinese, the number of our compatriots who have died overseas over the years is at least several times that number. Therefore, the total number of overseas Chinese who have sacrificed themselves to overseas endeavors is in the tens of millions. Further, if we compare the number of overseas Chinese with the amount of money earned, even using the highest figures, the annual remittances sent back to China by overseas Chinese are only 200 million yuan (in fact, this figure only lasted for three or two years). For 10 million people, the money earned each year is 200 million yuan, averaging only 20 yuan per person per year. Considering the long hours of labor that overseas Chinese work each day, which is longer than any other nation, the actual reward of 20 yuan per year means that each overseas Chinese person working in their place of residence for a year is worth 20 yuan. Those who advocate anti-Chinese sentiment should realize this.

Because of misunderstandings between people, many tragedies have been created in history. The anti-Chinese incident must also be said to be one of the unfortunate events caused by misunderstandings between people. We sincerely hope that the concept of anti-Chinese sentiment will be corrected. This is not only our hope, but also a crucial matter that cannot be ignored by various countries in the world.

Regarding the latter, the achievements of the overseas Chinese are by no means accidental or forceful. What the overseas Chinese have gained is not a high price, and it is certainly not a unilateral benefit. If people do not forget historical facts and neglect the interdependent conditions of human existence, the concept of anti-Chinese sentiment will not arise, nor will everyone suffer harm. Originally, many people know the historical facts of overseas Chinese migration to various places, but for the sake of clarity, we will briefly review them:

(1) The Period of Transportation and Visits: Zhang Qian's travels to the Western Regions during the Han Dynasty, Ma Yuan's visit to Jiaozhi, the monk Faxian's journey to the south during the Jin Dynasty, and Zheng He's voyages are all examples of the period of transportation and visits.

(2) The Period of Political Migration: From the Ming to the Qing Dynasties, many Chinese people migrated overseas due to political instability. National laws prohibited emigration, and the Qing Dynasty continued to strictly enforce the ban. This is the period of political migration.

(3) The Period of Commerce and Trade: From the 16th to the 19th centuries, both England and the Netherlands adopted a policy of free immigration to develop barren lands. They actively recruited Chinese laborers and even forcibly transported them to work. In the early 19th century, gold mines were discovered in California and other places in the United States, and the construction of roads required a large number of Chinese laborers. South America also recruited Chinese laborers at this time. It was not until after 1815 that our country temporarily entered into explicit agreements with England, France, and other countries, allowing Chinese citizens to freely emigrate overseas. This can be said to be the period of commerce and trade.

What deserves our attention most is the third period, the period of commerce and trade, because this period was the peak of overseas Chinese development, as well as the period of greatest sacrifice and contribution by overseas Chinese. For example, in the 16th century, the Dutch, due to a lack of suitable labor for developing Southeast Asia, resorted to various means to recruit Chinese laborers. The most peculiar of these was the buying and selling and forced abduction of "piglets" (Chinese laborers). In 1623, the first governor-general of the Dutch East Indies, Coen, wrote a letter to his successor, saying:

"Batavia, Moluccas, Ambon, Banten, need a lot of manpower... There is no one in the world more suitable for our use than the Chinese... If trade cannot be obtained through friendship, now that the weather is good, warships can be sent to the ports of China to capture as many men, women, and children as possible... It is especially necessary to capture many Chinese..."

From the above letter, it can be seen that at that time, the colonial government did not hesitate to use plunder to forcibly bring Chinese people to work in order to develop Southeast Asia. Southeast Asia was like this, and the development of Brazil, Peru, Australia, and other places was not much different, using the method of transporting "piglets." Although a British person once said, "Without the overseas Chinese, there would probably be no Malaysia today," the overseas Chinese do not feel proud or happy when they hear this sentence. Instead, they feel a wave of sadness, which makes them recall the painful experiences of our overseas Chinese ancestors opening up the land from a bloody path.

According to page 180 of the General History of Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, in the early days of developing a certain mountain field in Southeast Asia, it was estimated that it would take about half a year to complete the work. Therefore, 50 "piglets" (Chinese laborers) were recruited. Unexpectedly, within half a year, only two survived. The other 48 died due to labor and disease. Since the reclamation of the mountain field was less than halfway completed, another 50 "piglets" were recruited to fill the ranks. After another half a year, the work was finally completed, but only 14 of the second batch of "piglets" survived. In total, 100 "piglets" were used to develop one mountain field, and 84 died in one year. If we add up the various mountain fields that have been developed in Southeast Asia, Central and South America, Australia, and other places, then the number of overseas Chinese lives sacrificed is probably not something that any monetary figure can express. If we do not observe the history of the colonial development of overseas Chinese struggling and sacrificing, we will not understand the inside story of the modern economic prosperity process.

The contribution of overseas Chinese to the local development and prosperity is clear from the historical process described above. It seems that those who advocate anti-Chinese sentiment should take a break. However, now that human competition is moving further and further down the path of contradiction, the treatment of overseas Chinese in some places has been turned upside down. We also believe that today's advocates of anti-Chinese sentiment are not completely illiterate, but they have neglected the interdependent conditions of human existence, leading to the misunderstanding that the efforts of the overseas Chinese are "forceful seizure" rather than a "living gift" to the local community. We hope they will eventually have the opportunity to understand this clearly. (To be continued)

Local News

The "Harvard" Sunk After Collision Yesterday Morning

Importing Foreign Rice from Siam

On the Jiangmian River Surface in Lujiazui, Pudong

Head-On Collision with the "Tongde"

Cargo Lost, Crew Safe

The Norwegian ship "Harvard," Herver, represented by Messageries Maritimes, No. 6 Sichuan Road, agent of Hong Kong's Ng Kwong Tsi Lung, was carrying 16,500 bags of foreign rice, totaling 1,700 tons, from Bangkok, Siam. The rice was purchased by local Chinese merchants. The ship first arrived in Hong Kong and then came to Shanghai. At 7:15 a.m. yesterday, the ship arrived at Wusong and immediately entered the port, sailing into the Huangpu River, preparing to unload at the Yitai Hing Wharf. At 8:45 a.m., when it reached the Jiangmian River surface in Lujiazui, opposite the Waibaidu Bridge, it collided with the "Tongde," represented by Taifoo Co., Hankou Road, resulting in a tragic sinking.

Collision of Two Ships: The "Tongde" was an empty ship yesterday morning, heading from Shanghai to Qingdao to load coal. At 8:45 a.m., it reached the Jiangmian River surface in Lujiazui, heading north from the south and turning east. The "Harvard" was heading west from the east and turning south. The two ships then collided. It was found that the current was strongest at that point, and it was also high tide. When the "Tongde" and "Harvard" approached each other, neither side sounded the whistle. In a split second, the bow of the "Tongde" violently collided with the left side of the "Harvard's" fore cabin, resulting in the disaster.

The "Harvard" Sinks: A large hole was punched on the left side of the bow of the "Harvard," the damage was below the waterline of the cargo hold. River water immediately rushed into the fore cabin, and the bow immediately sank. Further, because it was fully loaded with foreign rice, the pressure was too great, and the ship lost its buoyancy. In a short time, the second, third, and fourth cabins were also flooded. In less than half an hour, it sank on the Jiangmian River surface in Lujiazui. Initially, the entire upper deck was still visible above the water, but by the afternoon, the upper decks of the front and middle cabins had also submerged, with only the stern of the ship visible in the Huangpu River.

Crew Rescued: After the accident, the Jianghai Customs and Lujiazui Water Police Station urgently dispatched the "Lihai Jinghui" small steam launch and sampans to Lujiazui. They first rescued 31 stokers from the "Harvard," as well as the captain, first and second officers, and engineers, a total of 13 people, and temporarily housed them in the police station. Later, Ng Kwong Tsi Lung's Shanghai office and Messageries Maritimes manager Tsang Kwong-king arranged to accommodate the crew temporarily in local Shanghai hotels, awaiting telegrams from the shipowner to determine the next course of action. Therefore, all the crew and sailors of the "Harvard" were unharmed.

Ship Body Towed to Shore: After Messageries Maritimes received the accident report of the "Harvard," Tsang Kwong-king immediately consulted Jardine Matheson, who dispatched two tugboats to Lujiazui. Because the area is a major waterway for ships, the sunken "Harvard" was significantly obstructing navigation. Therefore, during high tide, the tugboats gradually towed the ship to a shallower area on the Pudong bank near the Chunjiang Wharf on the side of the Lujiazui Water Police Station and ran it aground. The tugboats were positioned on either side of the sunken ship to prevent it from sinking into the center of the river.

Sunken Ship Markers: Navigation for ships in the area of the sunken "Harvard" was quite inconvenient. The crew immediately hoisted four green flags on the tops of the two masts to provide a warning. At night, red lights were hung to avoid collisions with passing ships. The municipal ferries on the Chunjiang line were forced to detour because the exit from the Chunjiang Wharf in Pudong was blocked by the sunken ship, making travel even more inconvenient at night.

Inspectors Dispatched: After receiving the report about the "Harvard," Messageries Maritimes immediately dispatched Deputy Manager Li Zhi-yi to Taifoo Co. to order a surveyor to go to the site to investigate and devise a method to salvage the rice loaded in the ship. After receiving the report, Taifoo Co. immediately dispatched a surveyor to the site of the accident in Lujiazui. The matter of determining responsibility for the collision will be handled after the surveyor's report. The two parties will need to hire impartial inspectors and summon the crews of both ships for questioning before a determination can be made. At present, it cannot be determined, so neither party is willing to make any statements.

Amount of Losses: The "Harvard" was registered as 761 tons, with a cargo capacity of 2,000 tons. It was built in 1921 by the Shanghai Ruirong Shipyard and was 242 feet and 7 inches long, 37 feet and 2 inches wide, and 15 feet deep. The single-deck cabin was owned by a Norwegian merchant and was leased to Ng Kwong Tsi Lung's timber firm to load 1,600 tons of Bangkok rice, approximately 16,500 bags, valued at over 200,000 yuan. The ship itself was worth over 200,000 yuan, for a total loss of over 400,000 yuan. The losses of the "Tongde" are not included. The "Harvard's" hull was insured for 200,000 yuan in Norway by the Shanghai Norwegian firm Shun Heng Co., and the rice cargo was insured for 200,000 yuan by the British firm New Zealand Insurance Company. Messageries Maritimes has already notified Ng Kwong Tsi Lung's timber firm to inform the two insurance companies that insured the hull and cargo.

The scene when the "Harvard" sank (photo by Qichang)

Salvaging Rice: Messageries Maritimes believed that the rice was already soaked in water and that if it was not salvaged immediately, the ship would inevitably explode when the rice swelled. Therefore, yesterday morning, Jardine Matheson's tugboat company was asked to dispatch tugboats to salvage the rice. Starting at 10 a.m. yesterday, Jardine Matheson dispatched three large tugboats with cargo cranes and a large number of workers to the site to open the cargo hold doors and lift the rice. The "Harvard" is now leaning against the beach, with the deck submerged in water. Only the stern, smokestack, and flag are visible above the water. It is not expected to sink any further. Jardine Matheson's tugboats are parked beside the ship, working to salvage the rice. Water police officers have been dispatched to the scene. Many onlookers are on the shore. It is said that even if the waterlogged rice is salvaged, it cannot be eaten and can only be used to make alcohol, etc.

"Tongde" Suspended: The senior officers of the "Harvard" were Norwegian, and the junior officers were Chinese. The compradore was Lai Ying-xiang, for a total of 44 people. After seeing the ship sink, they immediately removed all their luggage, bedding, and important ship documents and went ashore. At the same time, the "Tongde" immediately suspended operations and attempted to provide assistance. However, the "Harvard" was heavily loaded, the river water had already entered, and the ship was gradually sinking, so there was nothing that could be done. Moreover, the bow of the "Tongde" was also damaged, the rivets had fallen out, and the bow was skewed. Although there was no major damage, it could not sail until it had been repaired. Therefore, it was forced to return to the No. 43 floating buoy at Gaochangmiao to moor and reported the collision to Taifoo Co., its agent.

He (Nie) landed today (the 17th), and after a brief rest, he will visit Song Ziwen, a member of the Standing Committee of the National Economic Council, for consultation. After that, he will travel to Xi'an to inspect the Jingwei Canal. After the inspection, he will travel to Hebei, Shandong, and Henan to inspect the Yellow River water conservancy project along the way before heading south to inspect the Yangtze River water conservancy.
